4. Helpers

helm/fullstack-app/templates/_helpers.tpl

{{- define "fullstack-app.name" -}}
{{- .Chart.Name -}}
{{- end -}}

{{- define "fullstack-app.fullname" -}}
{{- printf "%s-%s" .Release.Name .Chart.Name | trunc 63 | trimSuffix "-" -}}
{{- end -}}

{{- define "fullstack-app.labels" -}}
app.kubernetes.io/name: {{ include "fullstack-app.name" . }}
app.kubernetes.io/instance: {{ .Release.Name }}
app.kubernetes.io/version: {{ .Chart.AppVersion | quote }}
app.kubernetes.io/managed-by: {{ .Release.Service }}
helm.sh/chart: {{ printf "%s-%s" .Chart.Name .Chart.Version | quote }}
{{- end -}}

{{- define "fullstack-app.backend.image" -}}
{{- if .Values.backend.image.digest -}}
{{ .Values.backend.image.repository }}@{{ .Values.backend.image.digest }}
{{- else -}}
{{ .Values.backend.image.repository }}:{{ .Values.backend.image.tag }}
{{- end -}}
{{- end -}}

{{- define "fullstack-app.frontend.image" -}}
{{- if .Values.frontend.image.digest -}}
{{ .Values.frontend.image.repository }}@{{ .Values.frontend.image.digest }}
{{- else -}}
{{ .Values.frontend.image.repository }}:{{ .Values.frontend.image.tag }}
{{- end -}}
{{- end -}}


---

5. Backend ServiceAccount

helm/fullstack-app/templates/backend-serviceaccount.yaml

{{- if .Values.backend.serviceAccount.create }}
apiVersion: v1
kind: ServiceAccount
metadata:
  name: {{ .Values.backend.serviceAccount.name }}
  namespace: {{ .Values.namespace.name }}
  labels:
    {{- include "fullstack-app.labels" . | nindent 4 }}
    app.kubernetes.io/component: backend
  annotations:
    {{- toYaml .Values.backend.serviceAccount.annotations | nindent 4 }}
{{- end }}


---

6. Backend Deployment

helm/fullstack-app/templates/backend-deployment.yaml

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: {{ include "fullstack-app.fullname" . }}-backend
  namespace: {{ .Values.namespace.name }}
  labels:
    {{- include "fullstack-app.labels" . | nindent 4 }}
    app.kubernetes.io/component: backend
spec:
  replicas: {{ .Values.backend.replicaCount }}
  revisionHistoryLimit: 10
  strategy:
    type: {{ .Values.backend.updateStrategy.type }}
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: {{ .Values.backend.updateStrategy.rollingUpdate.maxUnavailable }}
      maxSurge: {{ .Values.backend.updateStrategy.rollingUpdate.maxSurge }}
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app.kubernetes.io/name: {{ include "fullstack-app.name" . }}
      app.kubernetes.io/instance: {{ .Release.Name }}
      app.kubernetes.io/component: backend
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        {{- include "fullstack-app.labels" . | nindent 8 }}
        app.kubernetes.io/component: backend
    spec:
      serviceAccountName: {{ .Values.backend.serviceAccount.name }}
      automountServiceAccountToken: true
      terminationGracePeriodSeconds: {{ .Values.backend.terminationGracePeriodSeconds }}
      securityContext:
        {{- toYaml .Values.backend.podSecurityContext | nindent 8 }}
      containers:
        - name: backend
          image: {{ include "fullstack-app.backend.image" . }}
          imagePullPolicy: {{ .Values.global.imagePullPolicy }}
          ports:
            - name: http
              containerPort: {{ .Values.backend.service.targetPort }}
              protocol: TCP
          env:
            - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
              value: {{ .Values.backend.env.DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE | quote }}
            - name: PORT
              value: {{ .Values.backend.env.PORT | quote }}
            - name: DB_HOST
              valueFrom:
                secretKeyRef:
                  name: {{ .Values.backend.secretRefs.app }}
                  key: DB_HOST
            - name: DB_NAME
              valueFrom:
                secretKeyRef:
                  name: {{ .Values.backend.secretRefs.app }}
                  key: DB_NAME
            - name: DB_USER
              valueFrom:
                secretKeyRef:
                  name: {{ .Values.backend.secretRefs.app }}
                  key: DB_USER
            - name: DB_PASSWORD
              valueFrom:
                secretKeyRef:
                  name: {{ .Values.backend.secretRefs.app }}
                  key: DB_PASSWORD
            - name: DJANGO_SECRET_KEY
              valueFrom:
                secretKeyRef:
                  name: {{ .Values.backend.secretRefs.app }}
                  key: DJANGO_SECRET_KEY
          securityContext:
            {{- toYaml .Values.backend.securityContext | nindent 12 }}
          readinessProbe:
            httpGet:
              path: {{ .Values.backend.probes.readiness.path }}
              port: http
            initialDelaySeconds: {{ .Values.backend.probes.readiness.initialDelaySeconds }}
            periodSeconds: {{ .Values.backend.probes.readiness.periodSeconds }}
            timeoutSeconds: {{ .Values.backend.probes.readiness.timeoutSeconds }}
            failureThreshold: {{ .Values.backend.probes.readiness.failureThreshold }}
          livenessProbe:
            httpGet:
              path: {{ .Values.backend.probes.liveness.path }}
              port: http
            initialDelaySeconds: {{ .Values.backend.probes.liveness.initialDelaySeconds }}
            periodSeconds: {{ .Values.backend.probes.liveness.periodSeconds }}
            timeoutSeconds: {{ .Values.backend.probes.liveness.timeoutSeconds }}
            failureThreshold: {{ .Values.backend.probes.liveness.failureThreshold }}
          startupProbe:
            httpGet:
              path: {{ .Values.backend.probes.startup.path }}
              port: http
            initialDelaySeconds: {{ .Values.backend.probes.startup.initialDelaySeconds }}
            periodSeconds: {{ .Values.backend.probes.startup.periodSeconds }}
            timeoutSeconds: {{ .Values.backend.probes.startup.timeoutSeconds }}
            failureThreshold: {{ .Values.backend.probes.startup.failureThreshold }}
          resources:
            {{- toYaml .Values.backend.resources | nindent 12 }}
      {{- if .Values.backend.topologySpreadConstraints.enabled }}
      topologySpreadConstraints:
        - maxSkew: 1
          topologyKey: topology.kubernetes.io/zone
          whenUnsatisfiable: DoNotSchedule
          labelSelector:
            matchLabels:
              app.kubernetes.io/name: {{ include "fullstack-app.name" . }}
              app.kubernetes.io/instance: {{ .Release.Name }}
              app.kubernetes.io/component: backend
      {{- end }}


---

10. Frontend Deployment

helm/fullstack-app/templates/frontend-deployment.yaml

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: {{ include "fullstack-app.fullname" . }}-frontend
  namespace: {{ .Values.namespace.name }}
  labels:
    {{- include "fullstack-app.labels" . | nindent 4 }}
    app.kubernetes.io/component: frontend
spec:
  replicas: {{ .Values.frontend.replicaCount }}
  revisionHistoryLimit: 10
  strategy:
    type: {{ .Values.frontend.updateStrategy.type }}
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: {{ .Values.frontend.updateStrategy.rollingUpdate.maxUnavailable }}
      maxSurge: {{ .Values.frontend.updateStrategy.rollingUpdate.maxSurge }}
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app.kubernetes.io/name: {{ include "fullstack-app.name" . }}
      app.kubernetes.io/instance: {{ .Release.Name }}
      app.kubernetes.io/component: frontend
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        {{- include "fullstack-app.labels" . | nindent 8 }}
        app.kubernetes.io/component: frontend
    spec:
      serviceAccountName: {{ .Values.frontend.serviceAccount.name }}
      automountServiceAccountToken: false
      terminationGracePeriodSeconds: {{ .Values.frontend.terminationGracePeriodSeconds }}
      securityContext:
        {{- toYaml .Values.frontend.podSecurityContext | nindent 8 }}
      containers:
        - name: frontend
          image: {{ include "fullstack-app.frontend.image" . }}
          imagePullPolicy: {{ .Values.global.imagePullPolicy }}
          ports:
            - name: http
              containerPort: {{ .Values.frontend.service.targetPort }}
              protocol: TCP
          securityContext:
            {{- toYaml .Values.frontend.securityContext | nindent 12 }}
          readinessProbe:
            httpGet:
              path: {{ .Values.frontend.probes.readiness.path }}
              port: http
            initialDelaySeconds: {{ .Values.frontend.probes.readiness.initialDelaySeconds }}
            periodSeconds: {{ .Values.frontend.probes.readiness.periodSeconds }}
            timeoutSeconds: {{ .Values.frontend.probes.readiness.timeoutSeconds }}
            failureThreshold: {{ .Values.frontend.probes.readiness.failureThreshold }}
          livenessProbe:
            httpGet:
              path: {{ .Values.frontend.probes.liveness.path }}
              port: http
            initialDelaySeconds: {{ .Values.frontend.probes.liveness.initialDelaySeconds }}
            periodSeconds: {{ .Values.frontend.probes.liveness.periodSeconds }}
            timeoutSeconds: {{ .Values.frontend.probes.liveness.timeoutSeconds }}
            failureThreshold: {{ .Values.frontend.probes.liveness.failureThreshold }}
          resources:
            {{- toYaml .Values.frontend.resources | nindent 12 }}
      {{- if .Values.frontend.topologySpreadConstraints.enabled }}
      topologySpreadConstraints:
        - maxSkew: 1
          topologyKey: topology.kubernetes.io/zone
          whenUnsatisfiable: DoNotSchedule
          labelSelector:
            matchLabels:
              app.kubernetes.io/name: {{ include "fullstack-app.name" . }}
              app.kubernetes.io/instance: {{ .Release.Name }}
              app.kubernetes.io/component: frontend
      {{- end }}

14. Ingress

helm/fullstack-app/templates/ingress.yaml

{{- if .Values.ingress.enabled }}
apiVersion: networking.k8s.io/v1
kind: Ingress
metadata:
  name: {{ include "fullstack-app.fullname" . }}
  namespace: {{ .Values.namespace.name }}
  labels:
    {{- include "fullstack-app.labels" . | nindent 4 }}
  annotations:
    kubernetes.io/ingress.class: {{ .Values.ingress.className }}
    alb.ingress.kubernetes.io/scheme: {{ .Values.ingress.scheme }}
    alb.ingress.kubernetes.io/target-type: ip
    alb.ingress.kubernetes.io/certificate-arn: {{ .Values.ingress.certificateArn | quote }}
    alb.ingress.kubernetes.io/group.name: {{ .Values.ingress.groupName | quote }}
    alb.ingress.kubernetes.io/ssl-redirect: {{ .Values.ingress.sslRedirect | quote }}
    alb.ingress.kubernetes.io/healthcheck-path: {{ .Values.ingress.healthcheckPath | quote }}
    alb.ingress.kubernetes.io/listen-ports: '[{"HTTP":80},{"HTTPS":443}]'
    alb.ingress.kubernetes.io/load-balancer-attributes: {{ join "," (list
      (printf "idle_timeout.timeout_seconds=%s" (index .Values.ingress.albAttributes "idle_timeout.timeout_seconds"))
      (printf "routing.http.drop_invalid_header_fields.enabled=%s" (index .Values.ingress.albAttributes "routing.http.drop_invalid_header_fields.enabled"))
      (printf "access_logs.s3.enabled=%s" (index .Values.ingress.albAttributes "access_logs.s3.enabled"))
      (printf "access_logs.s3.bucket=%s" (index .Values.ingress.albAttributes "access_logs.s3.bucket"))
      (printf "access_logs.s3.prefix=%s" (index .Values.ingress.albAttributes "access_logs.s3.prefix"))
    ) | quote }}
    alb.ingress.kubernetes.io/wafv2-acl-arn: {{ .Values.ingress.wafAclArn | quote }}
spec:
  ingressClassName: {{ .Values.ingress.className }}
  rules:
    {{- range .Values.ingress.hosts }}
    - host: {{ .host | quote }}
      http:
        paths:
          {{- range .paths }}
          - path: {{ .path }}
            pathType: {{ .pathType }}
            backend:
              service:
                name: {{ .serviceName }}
                port:
                  number: {{ .servicePort }}
          {{- end }}
    {{- end }}
{{- end }}

16. Backend NetworkPolicy

helm/fullstack-app/templates/backend-networkpolicy.yaml

{{- if .Values.networkPolicy.enabled }}
apiVersion: networking.k8s.io/v1
kind: NetworkPolicy
metadata:
  name: backend-allow
  namespace: {{ .Values.namespace.name }}
spec:
  podSelector:
    matchLabels:
      app.kubernetes.io/component: backend
      app.kubernetes.io/instance: {{ .Release.Name }}
  policyTypes:
    - Ingress
    - Egress
  ingress:
    - from:
        - podSelector:
            matchLabels:
              app.kubernetes.io/component: frontend
              app.kubernetes.io/instance: {{ .Release.Name }}
        - namespaceSelector:
            matchLabels:
              kubernetes.io/metadata.name: kube-system
      ports:
        - protocol: TCP
          port: 8000
  egress:
    - to:
        - ipBlock:
            cidr: 10.10.20.0/24
        - ipBlock:
            cidr: 10.10.21.0/24
        - ipBlock:
            cidr: 10.10.22.0/24
      ports:
        - protocol: TCP
          port: 5432
    - to:
        - namespaceSelector:
            matchLabels:
              kubernetes.io/metadata.name: kube-system
      ports:
        - protocol: UDP
          port: 53
        - protocol: TCP
          port: 53
{{- end }}

20. Namespace manifest

gitops-repo/clusters/prod/namespaces/app-prod.yaml

apiVersion: v1
kind: Namespace
metadata:
  name: app-prod
  labels:
    environment: prod
    istio-injection: disabled
    pod-security.kubernetes.io/enforce: restricted
    pod-security.kubernetes.io/audit: restricted
    pod-security.kubernetes.io/warn: restricted

21. GitOps application values structure

gitops-repo/apps/fullstack-app/base/values-common.yaml

deploymentStrategy:
  mode: rollingUpdate

networkPolicy:
  enabled: true
  defaultDeny: true

externalSecrets:
  enabled: true

serviceMonitor:
  enabled: true

gitops-repo/apps/fullstack-app/overlays/prod/values.yaml

global:
  environment: prod
namespace:
  name: app-prod

backend:
  image:
    tag: "2.8.4-a1b2c3d"

frontend:
  image:
    tag: "2.8.4-a1b2c3d"


---

22. Blue/Green option pattern

For full Blue/Green, the clean enterprise pattern is usually done with Argo Rollouts or service switching with distinct selectors.

Illustrative service split:

apiVersion: v1
kind: Service
metadata:
  name: backend-active
  namespace: app-prod
spec:
  selector:
    app.kubernetes.io/component: backend
    release-color: blue
  ports:
    - port: 8000
      targetPort: 8000

And alternate deployment:

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: fullstack-app-backend-green
  namespace: app-prod
spec:
  replicas: 4
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app.kubernetes.io/component: backend
      release-color: green
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app.kubernetes.io/component: backend
        release-color: green

Traffic flips by changing the selector on backend-active or via a rollout controller.


---

23. Canary option pattern

Illustrative weighted canary with Argo Rollouts:

apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
kind: Rollout
metadata:
  name: backend-rollout
  namespace: app-prod
spec:
  replicas: 4
  strategy:
    canary:
      steps:
        - setWeight: 10
        - pause:
            duration: 5m
        - setWeight: 25
        - pause:
            duration: 10m
        - setWeight: 50
        - pause:
            duration: 15m
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app.kubernetes.io/component: backend
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app.kubernetes.io/component: backend
    spec:
      containers:
        - name: backend
          image: 123456789012.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/fullstack-platform/backend:2.8.5-f9e8d7c

That is not the default path, but it is the correct enterprise extension path.


---

F. Line-by-line explanation of critical sections

Chart metadata

apiVersion: v2

Helm 3 chart format.

version

This is the chart version, not the app version. It changes when the packaging changes.

appVersion

This is a user-facing version reference for the app release.

Important distinction:

chart version tracks manifest packaging evolution

app version tracks application release



---

Values structure

namespace.create: false

In mature GitOps setups, namespaces are often created by platform bootstrap, not application charts.

Why:

namespace lifecycle is a platform concern

security labels, quotas, and policies are easier to manage centrally



---

image.tag and image.digest

Both are supported intentionally.

Why:

lower environments often promote by immutable version tag

production can pin by digest for stronger release integrity


If digest is set, the helper renders repository@sha256:... and ignores tag.

That is a strong production pattern.


---

resources.requests and limits

This satisfies the requirement and is critical.

Why:

requests influence scheduling

limits bound resource consumption

HPA behavior becomes meaningful

cost and stability improve


Without requests, Kubernetes cannot schedule intelligently. Without limits, a bad process can create noisy neighbor issues.


---

autoscaling

HPA is based on CPU and memory in this example because it is broadly supported and practical.

Enterprise note: For Django APIs, CPU + request latency + queue depth often produce better autoscaling signals than CPU alone. But CPU/memory is a credible baseline.


---

pdb.minAvailable

This protects availability during:

node drains

cluster upgrades

voluntary disruptions

autoscaler consolidation


Example: If prod has 4 replicas and minAvailable: 3, Kubernetes will not allow voluntary disruption to reduce healthy pods below 3.


---

maxUnavailable: 0

This is important for zero-downtime rolling updates.

It means:

do not take down an existing ready pod before a replacement is available


Combined with readiness probes and enough cluster capacity, this materially reduces deployment risk.


---

maxSurge: 1

Allows one extra pod above desired count during rollout.

That enables a safe handoff:

bring up replacement

wait for readiness

then terminate old pod



---

terminationGracePeriodSeconds

This allows the app to stop cleanly.

For Django/Gunicorn:

finish in-flight requests

close connections cleanly

avoid request drops during rollout


Too short a value causes user-facing errors during deploys.


---

Security context

Pod-level seccompProfile: RuntimeDefault

This applies the container runtime’s default seccomp profile, reducing syscall exposure.

A strong baseline control.


---

Container-level controls

runAsNonRoot: true
allowPrivilegeEscalation: false
readOnlyRootFilesystem: true
capabilities:
  drop:
    - ALL

These are core workload hardening settings.

What each does:

runAsNonRoot: container cannot run as UID 0

allowPrivilegeEscalation: false: blocks gaining more privilege through binaries/setuid

readOnlyRootFilesystem: true: prevents mutation of the image filesystem

drop: ALL: removes Linux capabilities not explicitly required


This is exactly what security teams expect for modern workloads.


---

Backend probes

startupProbe

Protects slow-starting applications from premature liveness kills.

This is especially useful for Django apps that may take longer on startup due to:

migrations checks

static initialization

dependency warming

app import overhead


Without startup probe, liveness can cause restart loops during cold starts.


---

readinessProbe

This controls whether a pod receives traffic.

For Django, readiness should reflect dependency health enough to serve requests safely. In the example, /readyz is separate from /healthz, which is a best practice.


---

livenessProbe

This determines whether the app should be restarted.

Liveness should be cheap and not dependency-heavy, otherwise external dependency blips can cause unnecessary pod restarts.


---

ServiceAccount and IRSA annotations

eks.amazonaws.com/role-arn

This binds the Kubernetes ServiceAccount to an AWS IAM role via IRSA.

Why:

pod-level least privilege

no static AWS credentials

avoids node-wide over-permissioning


In this app, the backend is more likely than the frontend to need AWS API access, for example:

Secrets retrieval through External Secrets controller path

S3 access for media or exports

SQS/SNS integration

KMS usage through SDK path



---

automountServiceAccountToken

Backend = true

Kept enabled if the pod may need in-cluster identity and token-based integrations.

Frontend = false

Safer default because the frontend static server typically does not need Kubernetes API access.

This is the kind of detail that signals maturity.


---

Topology spread constraints

topologyKey: topology.kubernetes.io/zone
whenUnsatisfiable: DoNotSchedule

This encourages pods to spread across AZs.

Why:

improved resilience to AZ failure

reduces concentration risk

aligns with multi-AZ architecture


This is a stronger availability posture than relying on scheduler luck.


---

ALB ingress annotations

alb.ingress.kubernetes.io/target-type: ip

With EKS and VPC CNI, IP target type is often preferred because it registers pod IPs directly rather than node ports.

Benefits:

better traffic path

cleaner scaling behavior

less node indirection



---

certificate-arn

TLS is terminated at the ALB using ACM-managed certificates.

Enterprise norm.


---

wafv2-acl-arn

Associates the ingress with AWS WAF, giving a place for managed rules and application-specific protections.

Strong production pattern for internet-facing apps.


---

ALB access logs

These are essential for:

forensic analysis

request path debugging

traffic review

security evidence



---

NetworkPolicy

Default deny

podSelector: {}
policyTypes:
  - Ingress
  - Egress

This means no pod communicates unless explicitly allowed.

That is the correct secure-by-default model.


---

Backend allow policy

Only allows:

ingress from frontend and required system sources

egress to DB subnet ranges on 5432

DNS egress


Enterprise refinement: For production, I would usually avoid broad namespace allowances unless clearly justified. The example remains readable while still being realistic.


---

Frontend allow policy

Only allows:

ingress from cluster/system path that fronts ALB traffic

egress to backend

DNS egress


This sharply reduces lateral movement options.


---

ExternalSecret

This bridges AWS Secrets Manager into Kubernetes as synced Secrets.

Why this matters:

no hardcoded secrets

no secrets in Helm values

rotation-friendly

works well with GitOps because only references are in Git, not secret values


This is fully aligned with the requirement.


---

ServiceMonitor

This allows Prometheus Operator to discover and scrape backend metrics.

Why:

observability should be declared with the workload

metrics scraping becomes standardized and reviewable

golden signals and SLOs become easier later



---

Blue/Green and Canary design

Rolling update as default

Best default for most services if:

readiness is solid

resources are correct

app is backward-compatible during transition


Blue/Green

Use when:

release risk is higher

cutover needs stronger control

rollback must be nearly instantaneous

environment parity is good enough to run two full versions briefly


Canary

Use when:

you want to expose a subset of traffic first

you have strong metrics and alerting

you want automated progression gates later


This is the right maturity ladder.


---

G. Commands to run

1. Validate chart rendering for dev

helm template fullstack-app ./helm/fullstack-app \
  -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values.yaml \
  -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values-dev.yaml

What it does

renders the Helm chart locally

merges base values with dev overrides

prints generated Kubernetes manifests without applying them


Useful for review, CI validation, and debugging template logic.


---

2. Validate chart rendering for prod

helm template fullstack-app ./helm/fullstack-app \
  -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values.yaml \
  -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values-prod.yaml

What it does

Renders the exact prod manifest set that GitOps would eventually apply.


---

3. Lint the chart

helm lint ./helm/fullstack-app

What it does

Checks:

chart structure

template syntax

obvious misconfigurations


This should run in CI on every change.


---

4. Dry-run install against cluster context

helm upgrade --install fullstack-app ./helm/fullstack-app \
  --namespace app-dev \
  --create-namespace \
  -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values.yaml \
  -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values-dev.yaml \
  --dry-run

What it does

Simulates an install/upgrade without changing the cluster.

In this architecture, GitOps will own deployment, but this remains useful for local verification.


---

5. Show rendered manifests for a single template

helm template fullstack-app ./helm/fullstack-app \
  -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values.yaml \
  -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values-prod.yaml \
  --show-only templates/backend-deployment.yaml

What it does

Renders only the backend Deployment, which is useful when debugging rollout or security settings.


---

6. Verify Kubernetes schema with kubeconform or similar

helm template fullstack-app ./helm/fullstack-app \
  -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values.yaml \
  -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values-prod.yaml | kubeconform -strict -summary

---

Line-by-line explanation of Helm Management Commands:

1. helm lint ./helm/fullstack-app
   - Quality: Performs static analysis of the chart to catch syntax errors and missing vital metadata.

2. helm template ... -f values.yaml -f values-prod.yaml
   - Verification: Dry-renders the manifests to stdout using production overrides. Critical for pre-deployment diffing.

3. helm upgrade --install ... --create-namespace
   - idempotency: Ensures the application is either installed or updated to the desired state in a single, safe transaction.

4. kubeconform -strict -summary
   - Governance: Validates the rendered YAML against the formal Kubernetes OpenAPI schema to ensure the cluster will accept the resource.

---

What it does

renders manifests

validates them against Kubernetes schemas

catches invalid field shapes before merge


Strong enterprise CI practice.


---

7. Inspect diff before promotion

helm diff upgrade fullstack-app ./helm/fullstack-app \
  --namespace app-prod \
  -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values.yaml \
  -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values-prod.yaml

What it does

Shows exactly what would change between current and proposed release.

In GitOps, diffs are primarily Git-based, but local manifest diffing is still useful.


---

H. Production best practices

1. Keep charts readable

Do not turn Helm into a programming language. Prefer explicit values over deeply nested conditional magic.


---

2. Use one chart per release boundary

If backend and frontend are always deployed together, one chart is fine. If their lifecycles diverge materially, split them into separate charts later.


---

3. Pin images by digest in prod

Tags are okay for human reference, but digest pinning gives stronger release integrity.


---

4. Always define requests and limits

This is mandatory for reliability and cost control.


---

5. Separate readiness from liveness

Readiness determines traffic eligibility. Liveness determines restart behavior. They should not be identical unless justified.


---

6. Use startup probes for slower apps

This avoids false restarts during cold start.


---

7. Use PDBs for every critical workload

Otherwise voluntary disruptions during node upgrades can cause avoidable outages.


---

8. Spread pods across zones

Use topology spread constraints or anti-affinity, ideally both as needed.


---

9. Run with restricted pod security posture

Even before admission policies, the workload specs themselves should be hardened.


---

10. Default deny network traffic

Then open only what is needed. This is the correct secure baseline.


---

11. Keep namespaces managed centrally

Namespace labels, quotas, and pod security settings should usually be platform-owned.


---

12. Use IRSA for AWS access

Never inject static AWS credentials into pods.


---

13. Keep secrets out of values files

Helm values must not contain credentials.


---

14. Design for rollout evolution

Start with rolling updates, but leave room for canary and Blue/Green where risk or maturity justifies it.


---

15. Monitor every production service

Metrics exposure and ServiceMonitor integration should be standard, not optional.


---

I. Common enterprise mistakes

1. Putting secrets in values.yaml

Huge anti-pattern. Secrets end up in Git, CI logs, and chart history.


---

2. No resource limits

This leads to unstable clusters and unpredictable cost.


---

3. No PDBs

Cluster upgrades then become user-visible incidents.


---

4. Default-allow networking

This makes lateral movement too easy and breaks least-privilege network design.


---

5. Root containers in Kubernetes

Even if the image runs, security review will flag it immediately.


---

6. Using identical health endpoints for everything without thought

Liveness, readiness, and startup serve different operational purposes.


---

7. Over-templating Helm charts

Too much abstraction makes charts impossible to review safely.


---

8. Treating namespaces as the only security boundary

They help, but real isolation also needs RBAC, NetworkPolicies, Pod Security, and IAM discipline.


---

9. No revision history

Rollback becomes weaker when deployment history is not retained.


---

10. No topology spread

Pods can cluster into one AZ and create hidden fragility.


---

11. GitOps repo with giant per-env copy-paste YAML sprawl

Better to keep reusable chart + clear overlays than duplicate entire manifests everywhere.


---

12. Exposing unnecessary service account tokens

Many pods do not need them.


---

J. Interview explanation (Senior/Principal level)

A strong Principal-level explanation would sound like this:

> I package the Django backend and React frontend with Helm using opinionated, security-hardened defaults and environment-specific values for dev, stage, and prod. Every pod has requests and limits, readiness/liveness probes, HPA, PDBs, non-root execution, restricted security contexts, and default-deny NetworkPolicies. Traffic enters through an ALB-backed ingress integrated with ACM and WAF. ServiceAccounts are IRSA-ready, secrets are sourced from AWS Secrets Manager through External Secrets, and the repo structure is designed for GitOps promotion. Rolling updates are the default, but the design supports Blue/Green and canary patterns for higher-risk releases.



Then deepen it.

What makes this Principal-level

1. You connect manifests to operational outcomes

You are not just listing YAML resources. You are explaining how each one affects:

availability

security

rollback safety

auditability

cost

scaling behavior



---

2. You understand workload hardening natively

A strong answer includes security controls in the pod specs themselves, not only in external guardrails.


---

3. You understand rollout engineering

A principal candidate clearly explains why:

maxUnavailable: 0

readiness probes

PDBs

topology spread

surge settings


all work together to make zero-downtime realistic.


---

4. You think in platform contracts

The chart is not just app packaging. It is a contract between:

application engineers

platform team

SRE

security

compliance

GitOps controller



---

5. You distinguish default path from advanced path

Default:

rolling updates


Advanced:

Blue/Green

canary with Argo Rollouts

progressive delivery with metrics gates


That is how mature platforms evolve.


---

How to explain zero-downtime from this layer

For zero-downtime rolling deployment to work safely, I would say all of the following must be true:

at least 2+ replicas, usually more in prod

readiness probe only goes green when pod can truly serve

maxUnavailable: 0

small positive surge

PDB prevents too much simultaneous disruption

enough spare cluster capacity or autoscaling headroom exists

app shutdown is graceful

schema changes are backward-compatible during the deployment window


That is a much stronger answer than simply saying “Kubernetes rolling updates give zero downtime.”


---

- Default: RollingUpdate
- Optional: Blue/Green
- Optional: Canary


---

Layer 3 outcome

After this layer is implemented, you have:

Helm-packaged workloads

namespace-based workload organization

environment-specific deployment values

hardened pod security settings

resource requests and limits on all pods

HPA on backend and frontend

PDBs for disruption safety

ALB ingress with TLS and WAF integration

default-deny NetworkPolicies

External Secrets integration for AWS Secrets Manager

topology-aware multi-AZ pod spread

GitOps-ready release structure

a clear path for rolling, Blue/Green, and canary deployments

4. CI Layer (Jenkins or equivalent)

A. What this layer/tool is

This layer is the build, verification, packaging, and release orchestration system for the application.

It takes source code changes and turns them into:

validated artifacts

scanned container images

SBOMs

provenance metadata

immutable ECR releases

GitOps repo updates for deployment promotion


For this architecture, the CI layer does not deploy directly to Kubernetes. It only:

builds

tests

scans

pushes to ECR

updates the GitOps repo


That separation is intentional and critical.

A realistic enterprise CI stack here is:

Jenkins as the orchestration engine

ephemeral containerized agents running on Kubernetes

shared libraries for standardized pipelines

integrated quality and security gates

ECR as the artifact registry

GitOps repo commit/PR as the deployment handoff


This layer is where the organization enforces artifact quality, release hygiene, and supply-chain policy before anything becomes deployable.


---

B. Why it is needed at this stage

Once infrastructure and Kubernetes packaging exist, the platform needs a controlled path to answer these questions every release:

Did the code compile?

Did unit tests pass?

Did linting pass?

Were container images built reproducibly?

Were vulnerabilities scanned?

Was an SBOM generated?

Was the artifact tagged immutably?

Was it pushed to ECR?

Was the GitOps repo updated correctly for the right environment?

Is there evidence for audit and rollback?


Without a mature CI layer, teams fall into unsafe patterns:

manual image building

inconsistent tags

skipped scans

direct cluster deploys

environment drift

missing provenance

weak rollback confidence


The CI layer is the supply-chain enforcement point.


---

C. Real-world enterprise reasoning

A Principal-level CI design is not just “run tests in Jenkins.” It is a release control system.

1. CI and CD should be separated

In GitOps platforms, CI should never run kubectl apply or helm upgrade directly against production clusters.

Why:

keeps deployment intent in Git

makes promotions reviewable

improves auditability

avoids Jenkins credentials having broad cluster admin power

reduces hidden out-of-band changes


So CI produces deployable artifacts and then updates the GitOps repo.


---

2. Every artifact must be traceable

A release should be traceable across:

source commit SHA

CI build number

image tag

image digest

SBOM

scan results

GitOps commit that promoted it


That traceability is what makes incident response and audit possible at scale.


---

3. Security scanning belongs in the critical path

At enterprise scale, image and dependency scanning cannot be “best effort.”

This layer should enforce:

dependency scanning

container image scanning

IaC and Helm linting where applicable

secret detection

SBOM generation


Not all issues should block every build identically, but the gating model must be defined.


---

4. Branching and promotion need discipline

A realistic promotion model:

feature branches → PR validation only

develop or integration branch → build and push to dev ECR tags, update dev GitOps overlay

release/* branch → update stage overlay after approval gates

main or tagged release → promote to prod via GitOps repo PR


The exact branching model varies, but the key is that promotion is a controlled metadata change, not “rebuild something differently.”


---

5. CI agents should be ephemeral

Long-lived Jenkins nodes accumulate:

drift

credentials

tool mismatch

hidden dependencies

security risk


Use ephemeral Kubernetes agents with controlled images and least privilege.


---

6. CI must be consistent across services

Platform teams should create shared pipeline primitives for:

Docker build

Trivy scan

SBOM generation

ECR auth

GitOps update

commit metadata standardization


This reduces pipeline sprawl and keeps quality gates consistent.


---

7. Multi-region matters in release flow

If the runtime is multi-region, image availability must also be multi-region.

Typical pattern:

push to primary ECR

use ECR replication or explicit push to secondary region

record digests for region-local registries if needed


CI must be designed with that in mind.


---

D. Folder structure

A realistic enterprise CI structure:

App repo

app-repo/
├── backend/
├── frontend/
├── helm/
├── Jenkinsfile
├── ci/
│   ├── scripts/
│   │   ├── set-version.sh
│   │   ├── build-backend.sh
│   │   ├── build-frontend.sh
│   │   ├── scan-image.sh
│   │   ├── generate-sbom.sh
│   │   ├── push-ecr.sh
│   │   ├── update-gitops.sh
│   │   └── verify-helm.sh
│   ├── trivy/
│   │   └── trivy.yaml
│   ├── sbom/
│   │   └── syft-config.yaml
│   ├── quality-gates/
│   │   └── policy.yaml
│   └── docker/
│       ├── backend-metadata.labels
│       └── frontend-metadata.labels
├── Makefile
└── docs/
    └── release-process.md

Jenkins shared library repo

jenkins-shared-library/
├── vars/
│   ├── pipelineInit.groovy
│   ├── dockerBuildAndScan.groovy
│   ├── ecrLogin.groovy
│   ├── gitopsPromote.groovy
│   └── slackNotify.groovy
├── src/
│   └── com/examplecorp/ci/
└── resources/

GitOps repo

gitops-repo/
├── apps/
│   └── fullstack-app/
│       ├── overlays/
│       │   ├── dev/values.yaml
│       │   ├── stage/values.yaml
│       │   └── prod/values.yaml
│       └── ...
└── ...

This keeps CI logic close to the app while centralizing reusable enterprise pipeline behaviors in a shared Jenkins library.


---

E. Copy-paste ready configuration files

1. Jenkinsfile

app-repo/Jenkinsfile

  }
}

---

Line-by-line Technical Commentary: Jenkinsfile

7051: pipeline {
- Orchestration: Defines the continuous integration logic as code, ensuring build consistency across the lifecycle.

7056: disableConcurrentBuilds()
- Safety: Critical for GitOps to prevent race conditions where two parallel builds try to push different versions to the same values layer simultaneously.

7343: /kaniko/executor ...
- Security: Builds OCI images without requiring a privileged Docker daemon, significantly hardening the CI agent's attack surface.

7426: trivy image --severity HIGH,CRITICAL --exit-code 1
- Governance: Implements a "Security Quality Gate" that blocks the release of any artifact with unpatched critical vulnerabilities.

7610: cleanWs()
- Hygiene: Automatically purges sensitive credentials (like SSH keys or Docker auth) from the ephemeral agent's disk after completion.

---
  agent none

  options {
    timestamps()
    disableConcurrentBuilds()
    buildDiscarder(logRotator(numToKeepStr: '50'))
    ansiColor('xterm')
    timeout(time: 60, unit: 'MINUTES')
  }

  environment {
    AWS_ACCOUNT_ID         = '123456789012'
    PRIMARY_REGION         = 'us-east-1'
    SECONDARY_REGION       = 'us-west-2'
    ECR_BACKEND_REPO       = 'fullstack-platform/backend'
    ECR_FRONTEND_REPO      = 'fullstack-platform/frontend'
    GITOPS_REPO_URL        = 'git@github.com:examplecorp/gitops-repo.git'
    APP_NAME               = 'fullstack-app'
    TRIVY_SEVERITY         = 'HIGH,CRITICAL'
    VERSION                = ''
    GIT_SHA_SHORT          = ''
    BACKEND_IMAGE_TAG      = ''
    FRONTEND_IMAGE_TAG     = ''
    BACKEND_IMAGE_URI      = ''
    FRONTEND_IMAGE_URI     = ''
    BACKEND_IMAGE_DIGEST   = ''
    FRONTEND_IMAGE_DIGEST  = ''
    TARGET_ENV             = ''
  }

  stages {
    stage('Init') {
      agent {
        kubernetes {
          label 'ci-init'
          defaultContainer 'jnlp'
          yaml """
apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
metadata:
  labels:
    job: ci-init
spec:
  serviceAccountName: jenkins-agent
  containers:
    - name: jnlp
      image: jenkins/inbound-agent:latest
      resources:
        requests:
          cpu: "100m"
          memory: "256Mi"
        limits:
          cpu: "500m"
          memory: "512Mi"
"""
        }
      }
      steps {
        checkout scm
        script {
          env.GIT_SHA_SHORT = sh(script: "git rev-parse --short=7 HEAD", returnStdout: true).trim()
          env.VERSION = sh(script: "./ci/scripts/set-version.sh", returnStdout: true).trim()
          env.BACKEND_IMAGE_TAG = "${env.VERSION}-${env.GIT_SHA_SHORT}"
          env.FRONTEND_IMAGE_TAG = "${env.VERSION}-${env.GIT_SHA_SHORT}"

          if (env.BRANCH_NAME == 'develop') {
            env.TARGET_ENV = 'dev'
          } else if (env.BRANCH_NAME == 'main') {
            env.TARGET_ENV = 'prod'
          } else if (env.BRANCH_NAME.startsWith('release/')) {
            env.TARGET_ENV = 'stage'
          } else {
            env.TARGET_ENV = 'pr'
          }

          env.BACKEND_IMAGE_URI = "${env.AWS_ACCOUNT_ID}.dkr.ecr.${env.PRIMARY_REGION}.amazonaws.com/${env.ECR_BACKEND_REPO}:${env.BACKEND_IMAGE_TAG}"
          env.FRONTEND_IMAGE_URI = "${env.AWS_ACCOUNT_ID}.dkr.ecr.${env.PRIMARY_REGION}.amazonaws.com/${env.ECR_FRONTEND_REPO}:${env.FRONTEND_IMAGE_TAG}"
        }
      }
    }

    stage('Lint and Unit Tests') {
      parallel {
        stage('Backend Quality') {
          agent {
            kubernetes {
              label 'backend-quality'
              defaultContainer 'python'
              yaml """
apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
spec:
  serviceAccountName: jenkins-agent
  containers:
    - name: python
      image: python:3.12-slim
      command: ['cat']
      tty: true
      resources:
        requests:
          cpu: "500m"
          memory: "1Gi"
        limits:
          cpu: "2"
          memory: "2Gi"
"""
            }
          }
          steps {
            checkout scm
            sh '''
              apt-get update
              apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends gcc libpq-dev
              python -m venv .venv
              . .venv/bin/activate
              pip install --upgrade pip
              pip install -r backend/app/requirements/dev.txt
              cd backend/app
              ruff check .
              black --check .
              pytest -q --maxfail=1 --disable-warnings
            '''
          }
        }

        stage('Frontend Quality') {
          agent {
            kubernetes {
              label 'frontend-quality'
              defaultContainer 'node'
              yaml """
apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
spec:
  serviceAccountName: jenkins-agent
  containers:
    - name: node
      image: node:22-bookworm-slim
      command: ['cat']
      tty: true
      resources:
        requests:
          cpu: "500m"
          memory: "1Gi"
        limits:
          cpu: "2"
          memory: "2Gi"
"""
            }
          }
          steps {
            checkout scm
            sh '''
              cd frontend
              npm ci
              npm run lint
              npm test -- --watchAll=false
              npm run build
            '''
          }
        }

        stage('Helm Validation') {
          agent {
            kubernetes {
              label 'helm-validate'
              defaultContainer 'helm'
              yaml """
apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
spec:
  serviceAccountName: jenkins-agent
  containers:
    - name: helm
      image: alpine/helm:3.15.4
      command: ['cat']
      tty: true
      resources:
        requests:
          cpu: "100m"
          memory: "256Mi"
        limits:
          cpu: "500m"
          memory: "512Mi"
"""
            }
          }
          steps {
            checkout scm
            sh '''
              helm lint ./helm/fullstack-app
              helm template fullstack-app ./helm/fullstack-app \
                -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values.yaml \
                -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values-dev.yaml >/tmp/dev-rendered.yaml
              helm template fullstack-app ./helm/fullstack-app \
                -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values.yaml \
                -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values-stage.yaml >/tmp/stage-rendered.yaml
              helm template fullstack-app ./helm/fullstack-app \
                -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values.yaml \
                -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values-prod.yaml >/tmp/prod-rendered.yaml
            '''
          }
        }
      }
    }

    stage('Security and Supply Chain') {
      parallel {
        stage('Filesystem Scan') {
          agent {
            kubernetes {
              label 'trivy-fs'
              defaultContainer 'trivy'
              yaml """
apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
spec:
  serviceAccountName: jenkins-agent
  containers:
    - name: trivy
      image: aquasec/trivy:0.53.0
      command: ['sh', '-c', 'sleep 3600']
      tty: true
      resources:
        requests:
          cpu: "200m"
          memory: "512Mi"
        limits:
          cpu: "1"
          memory: "1Gi"
"""
            }
          }
          steps {
            checkout scm
            sh '''
              trivy fs --scanners vuln,secret,config \
                --severity ${TRIVY_SEVERITY} \
                --exit-code 1 .
            '''
          }
        }

        stage('SBOM Source Prep') {
          agent {
            kubernetes {
              label 'syft-source'
              defaultContainer 'syft'
              yaml """
apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
spec:
  serviceAccountName: jenkins-agent
  containers:
    - name: syft
      image: anchore/syft:v1.12.0
      command: ['sh', '-c', 'sleep 3600']
      tty: true
      resources:
        requests:
          cpu: "100m"
          memory: "256Mi"
        limits:
          cpu: "500m"
          memory: "512Mi"
"""
            }
          }
          steps {
            checkout scm
            sh '''
              syft dir:. -o spdx-json > source-sbom.spdx.json
            '''
            archiveArtifacts artifacts: 'source-sbom.spdx.json', fingerprint: true
          }
        }
      }
    }

    stage('Build Images') {
      agent {
        kubernetes {
          label 'kaniko-build'
          defaultContainer 'kaniko'
          yaml """
apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
spec:
  serviceAccountName: jenkins-agent
  containers:
    - name: kaniko
      image: gcr.io/kaniko-project/executor:v1.23.2-debug
      command: ['sh', '-c', 'sleep 3600']
      tty: true
      volumeMounts:
        - name: docker-config
          mountPath: /kaniko/.docker
      resources:
        requests:
          cpu: "1"
          memory: "2Gi"
        limits:
          cpu: "4"
          memory: "6Gi"
  volumes:
    - name: docker-config
      projected:
        sources:
          - secret:
              name: ecr-docker-config
              items:
                - key: config.json
                  path: config.json
"""
        }
      }
      steps {
        checkout scm
        sh """
          /kaniko/executor \
            --context ${WORKSPACE} \
            --dockerfile ${WORKSPACE}/backend/Dockerfile \
            --destination ${BACKEND_IMAGE_URI} \
            --digest-file ${WORKSPACE}/backend-image.digest \
            --label org.opencontainers.image.version=${VERSION} \
            --label org.opencontainers.image.revision=${GIT_COMMIT} \
            --label org.opencontainers.image.source=${GIT_URL}

          /kaniko/executor \
            --context ${WORKSPACE} \
            --dockerfile ${WORKSPACE}/frontend/Dockerfile \
            --destination ${FRONTEND_IMAGE_URI} \
            --digest-file ${WORKSPACE}/frontend-image.digest \
            --label org.opencontainers.image.version=${VERSION} \
            --label org.opencontainers.image.revision=${GIT_COMMIT} \
            --label org.opencontainers.image.source=${GIT_URL}
        """
        script {
          env.BACKEND_IMAGE_DIGEST = sh(script: "cat backend-image.digest", returnStdout: true).trim()
          env.FRONTEND_IMAGE_DIGEST = sh(script: "cat frontend-image.digest", returnStdout: true).trim()
        }
        archiveArtifacts artifacts: '*image.digest', fingerprint: true
      }
    }

    stage('Image Scan and SBOM') {
      parallel {
        stage('Scan Backend Image') {
          agent {
            kubernetes {
              label 'trivy-image-backend'
              defaultContainer 'trivy'
              yaml """
apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
spec:
  serviceAccountName: jenkins-agent
  containers:
    - name: trivy
      image: aquasec/trivy:0.53.0
      command: ['sh', '-c', 'sleep 3600']
      tty: true
      resources:
        requests:
          cpu: "200m"
          memory: "512Mi"
        limits:
          cpu: "1"
          memory: "1Gi"
"""
            }
          }
          steps {
            sh '''
              trivy image --severity ${TRIVY_SEVERITY} --exit-code 1 ${BACKEND_IMAGE_URI}
            '''
          }
        }

        stage('Scan Frontend Image') {
          agent {
            kubernetes {
              label 'trivy-image-frontend'
              defaultContainer 'trivy'
              yaml """
apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
spec:
  serviceAccountName: jenkins-agent
  containers:
    - name: trivy
      image: aquasec/trivy:0.53.0
      command: ['sh', '-c', 'sleep 3600']
      tty: true
      resources:
        requests:
          cpu: "200m"
          memory: "512Mi"
        limits:
          cpu: "1"
          memory: "1Gi"
"""
            }
          }
          steps {
            sh '''
              trivy image --severity ${TRIVY_SEVERITY} --exit-code 1 ${FRONTEND_IMAGE_URI}
            '''
          }
        }

        stage('Generate Image SBOMs') {
          agent {
            kubernetes {
              label 'syft-image'
              defaultContainer 'syft'
              yaml """
apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
spec:
  serviceAccountName: jenkins-agent
  containers:
    - name: syft
      image: anchore/syft:v1.12.0
      command: ['sh', '-c', 'sleep 3600']
      tty: true
      resources:
        requests:
          cpu: "100m"
          memory: "256Mi"
        limits:
          cpu: "500m"
          memory: "512Mi"
"""
            }
          }
          steps {
            sh '''
              syft ${BACKEND_IMAGE_URI} -o spdx-json > backend-image-sbom.spdx.json
              syft ${FRONTEND_IMAGE_URI} -o spdx-json > frontend-image-sbom.spdx.json
            '''
            archiveArtifacts artifacts: '*sbom.spdx.json', fingerprint: true
          }
        }
      }
    }

    stage('Promote via GitOps') {
      when {
        expression { env.TARGET_ENV != 'pr' }
      }
      agent {
        kubernetes {
          label 'gitops-update'
          defaultContainer 'git'
          yaml """
apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
spec:
  serviceAccountName: jenkins-agent
  containers:
    - name: git
      image: alpine/git:2.45.2
      command: ['sh', '-c', 'sleep 3600']
      tty: true
      resources:
        requests:
          cpu: "100m"
          memory: "256Mi"
        limits:
          cpu: "500m"
          memory: "512Mi"
"""
        }
      }
      steps {
        withCredentials([sshUserPrivateKey(credentialsId: 'gitops-repo-ssh', keyFileVariable: 'SSH_KEY')]) {
          sh '''
            mkdir -p ~/.ssh
            cp ${SSH_KEY} ~/.ssh/id_rsa
            chmod 600 ~/.ssh/id_rsa
            ssh-keyscan github.com >> ~/.ssh/known_hosts

            git clone ${GITOPS_REPO_URL} gitops-repo
            cd gitops-repo

            yq -i '.backend.image.tag = "'"${BACKEND_IMAGE_TAG}"'"' apps/fullstack-app/overlays/${TARGET_ENV}/values.yaml
            yq -i '.frontend.image.tag = "'"${FRONTEND_IMAGE_TAG}"'"' apps/fullstack-app/overlays/${TARGET_ENV}/values.yaml
            yq -i '.backend.image.digest = "'"${BACKEND_IMAGE_DIGEST#sha256:}"'"' apps/fullstack-app/overlays/${TARGET_ENV}/values.yaml
            yq -i '.frontend.image.digest = "'"${FRONTEND_IMAGE_DIGEST#sha256:}"'"' apps/fullstack-app/overlays/${TARGET_ENV}/values.yaml

            git config user.email "jenkins@example.com"
            git config user.name "jenkins-ci"
            git checkout -b ci/promote-${APP_NAME}-${BUILD_NUMBER}
            git add apps/fullstack-app/overlays/${TARGET_ENV}/values.yaml
            git commit -m "Promote ${APP_NAME} to ${TARGET_ENV}: ${VERSION}-${GIT_SHA_SHORT}"
            git push origin HEAD
          '''
        }
      }
    }
  }

  post {
    always {
      junit allowEmptyResults: true, testResults: '**/junit*.xml'
      cleanWs()
    }
    success {
      echo "Build completed successfully"
    }
    failure {
      echo "Build failed"
    }
  }
}


---

2. Version generation script

ci/scripts/set-version.sh

#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail

if git describe --tags --exact-match >/dev/null 2>&1; then
  git describe --tags --exact-match | sed 's/^v//'
else
  DATE_PART="$(date -u +%Y.%m.%d)"
  BUILD_PART="${BUILD_NUMBER:-0}"
  echo "${DATE_PART}.${BUILD_PART}"
fi


---

3. Helm verification script

ci/scripts/verify-helm.sh

#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail

helm lint ./helm/fullstack-app

for env in dev stage prod; do
  helm template fullstack-app ./helm/fullstack-app \
    -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values.yaml \
    -f ./helm/fullstack-app/values-${env}.yaml >/tmp/${env}-rendered.yaml
done

4. Trivy baseline config

ci/trivy/trivy.yaml

timeout: 10m
format: table
exit-code: 1
ignore-unfixed: false
severity:
  - HIGH
  - CRITICAL
scanners:
  - vuln
  - secret
  - misconfig

5. SBOM generation script

ci/scripts/generate-sbom.sh

#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail

IMAGE_URI="$1"
OUTPUT_FILE="$2"

syft "${IMAGE_URI}" -o spdx-json > "${OUTPUT_FILE}"

---

Line-by-line Technical Commentary: CI Scripts

7558: set -euo pipefail
- Shell Hygiene: Ensures the script fails immediately on command failure (e), unset variables (u), or downstream pipe errors (o).

7561: git describe --tags --exact-match | sed 's/^v//'
- Versioning: Extracts the semantic version from the Git tag, removing the 'v' prefix for standard Helm compatibility.

7580: helm template fullstack-app ./helm/fullstack-app ...
- Validation: Iterates through all environments to ensure a single chart change doesn't break any specific environment's rendering.

7615: syft "${IMAGE_URI}" -o spdx-json > "${OUTPUT_FILE}"
- Compliance: Generates a Software Bill of Materials (SBOM) in SPDX format to satisfy security audits and supply chain visibility requirements.

---

6. Trivy image scan script

ci/scripts/scan-image.sh

#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail

IMAGE_URI="$1"

trivy image \
  --severity HIGH,CRITICAL \
  --exit-code 1 \
  "${IMAGE_URI}"

7. GitOps update script

ci/scripts/update-gitops.sh

#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail

GITOPS_DIR="$1"
TARGET_ENV="$2"
BACKEND_TAG="$3"
FRONTEND_TAG="$4"
BACKEND_DIGEST="$5"
FRONTEND_DIGEST="$6"

VALUES_FILE="${GITOPS_DIR}/apps/fullstack-app/overlays/${TARGET_ENV}/values.yaml"

yq -i ".backend.image.tag = \"${BACKEND_TAG}\"" "${VALUES_FILE}"
yq -i ".frontend.image.tag = \"${FRONTEND_TAG}\"" "${VALUES_FILE}"
yq -i ".backend.image.digest = \"${BACKEND_DIGEST#sha256:}\"" "${VALUES_FILE}"
yq -i ".frontend.image.digest = \"${FRONTEND_DIGEST#sha256:}\"" "${VALUES_FILE}"

    eks.amazonaws.com/role-arn: arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/jenkins-agent-irsa

9. Example IAM policy for Jenkins agent IRSA role

The actual role is provisioned by Terraform or platform bootstrap, but a realistic permissions boundary for ECR/GitOps-adjacent behavior might look like:

{
  "Version": "2012-10-17",
  "Statement": [
    {
      "Sid": "EcrPushPull",
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Action": [
        "ecr:GetAuthorizationToken",
        "ecr:BatchCheckLayerAvailability",
        "ecr:CompleteLayerUpload",
        "ecr:InitiateLayerUpload",
        "ecr:UploadLayerPart",
        "ecr:PutImage",
        "ecr:BatchGetImage",
        "ecr:DescribeImages"
      ],
      "Resource": "*"
    },
    {
      "Sid": "AllowReadOnlyMetadata",
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Action": [
        "sts:GetCallerIdentity"
      ],
      "Resource": "*"
    }
  ]
}

For a more mature setup, split permissions so build agents only access the repos they need.

10. Example Makefile targets for local CI parity

Makefile

.PHONY: backend-test frontend-test helm-verify trivy-fs

backend-test:
	cd backend/app && python -m pytest -q

frontend-test:
	cd frontend && npm ci && npm test -- --watchAll=false

helm-verify:
	./ci/scripts/verify-helm.sh

trivy-fs:
	trivy fs --scanners vuln,secret,config --severity HIGH,CRITICAL --exit-code 1 .


---

F. Line-by-line explanation of critical sections

Jenkins pipeline options

disableConcurrentBuilds()

Prevents overlapping runs of the same pipeline from stepping on each other.

Why:

avoids race conditions in shared branches

reduces tag confusion

prevents duplicate GitOps updates



---

buildDiscarder(logRotator(numToKeepStr: '50'))

Retains recent build history while preventing unbounded storage growth.

This matters for:

audit trail

troubleshooting

Jenkins storage cost control



---

timeout(time: 60, unit: 'MINUTES')

Protects against hung jobs and stale agents.

A good enterprise pipeline always bounds execution time.


---

Init stage

git rev-parse --short=7 HEAD

Creates a short commit identifier used in the immutable image tag.

This improves traceability.


---

VERSION = ./ci/scripts/set-version.sh

Separates release version logic from the Jenkinsfile.

That is cleaner and easier to standardize across repos.


---

Branch-to-environment mapping

if (env.BRANCH_NAME == 'develop') {
  env.TARGET_ENV = 'dev'
} else if (env.BRANCH_NAME == 'main') {
  env.TARGET_ENV = 'prod'
} else if (env.BRANCH_NAME.startsWith('release/')) {
  env.TARGET_ENV = 'stage'
}

This is a simple but realistic promotion policy.

Interpretation:

develop feeds dev

release/* feeds stage

main feeds prod

PR branches validate only


In some enterprises, prod promotion is tag-driven instead of branch-driven. That is also valid. The key is controlled promotion logic.


---

Ephemeral Kubernetes agents

Each stage runs in a short-lived pod.

Why this is important:

clean environment per stage

better isolation

easier scaling

fewer hidden dependencies

easier least-privilege model through IRSA


This is much better than static VM agents.


---

Parallel quality stages

Backend, frontend, and Helm validation run in parallel.

Benefits:

shorter feedback cycle

isolated failure domains

better resource scheduling


At enterprise scale, feedback speed materially affects developer productivity.


---

Backend quality stage

pip install -r backend/app/requirements/dev.txt

Installs dev/test tooling in the CI stage only, not in the runtime image.

Good separation of concerns.


---

ruff check .

Fast Python linting.

black --check .

Formatting enforcement.

pytest

Unit test gate.

This is the minimum serious baseline. Many enterprises also add:

coverage thresholds

import sorting

type checking with mypy

Django security checks



---

Frontend quality stage

npm ci

Deterministic install using lockfile.

This is important. npm install is weaker for CI reproducibility.


---

npm run lint, npm test, npm run build

This ensures the frontend:

passes static analysis

passes tests

actually compiles


A surprising number of pipelines skip the actual production build until too late.


---

Helm validation stage

This ensures:

chart syntax is valid

all env overlays render

obvious values/template breakage is caught before promotion


This is important in GitOps systems because broken Helm manifests can block ArgoCD syncs later.


---

Filesystem scan

trivy fs --scanners vuln,secret,config

This scans the source tree and config for:

dependency vulnerabilities

embedded secrets

configuration issues


This catches problems before image build.

That gives earlier feedback than image-only scanning.


---

SBOM source prep

Generating a source-level SBOM gives earlier package visibility, while later image-level SBOMs capture the final shipped artifact.

Enterprise reality: You often want both.


---

Kaniko image builds

Why Kaniko

In Kubernetes-based Jenkins agents, Kaniko avoids privileged Docker-in-Docker in many setups.

Benefits:

safer than exposing a Docker daemon

works well in container-native CI

well-known enterprise pattern



---

--digest-file

This is critical. It records the built image digest as emitted by the build itself.

That digest is then used for:

artifact evidence

GitOps updates

rollback

supply-chain traceability



---

OCI labels

--label org.opencontainers.image.version=${VERSION}
--label org.opencontainers.image.revision=${GIT_COMMIT}

These improve provenance.


---

Image scan and SBOM stage

Scanning the actual pushed image is mandatory because it is the real deployed artifact.

Why both source and image scanning matter:

source scanning finds issues earlier

image scanning finds final OS/package layer issues

together they cover more of the supply chain



---

GitOps promotion stage

This is one of the most important parts of the whole design.

It does not deploy directly

Instead, it:

clones the GitOps repo

updates the target environment values file

commits the new tag/digest references

pushes a branch for PR or merge workflow


This is the correct GitOps handoff.


---

yq -i

This updates YAML deterministically and safely in automation.

Avoid brittle sed hacks against YAML.


---

Why commit both tag and digest

The tag is useful for humans and dashboards. The digest is the real immutable artifact reference.

In stricter prod environments, the rendered chart may rely only on digest.


---

Artifact archiving

archiveArtifacts

Stores:

digest files

SBOMs

other build artifacts


Why:

audit evidence

incident response support

reproducibility

security investigations



---

Post block

cleanWs()

Removes workspace data to reduce leakage between builds.

Small detail, good hygiene.


---

G. Commands to run

1. Trigger Jenkins multibranch pipeline from SCM webhook

This is usually automatic, but operationally it means:

PR opened → validation build

merge to develop → dev promotion build

release branch update → stage promotion build

merge to main → prod promotion build



---

2. Run backend tests locally

cd backend/app
python -m venv .venv
. .venv/bin/activate
pip install -r requirements/dev.txt
ruff check .
black --check .
pytest -q --maxfail=1 --disable-warnings

What these commands do

create local Python environment

install development dependencies

run linting and formatting checks

run unit tests


This helps developers reproduce CI behavior locally.


---

3. Run frontend checks locally

cd frontend
npm ci
npm run lint
npm test -- --watchAll=false
npm run build

What these commands do

install exact locked dependencies

run lint rules

run tests

verify production build succeeds



---

4. Run Trivy filesystem scan locally

trivy fs --scanners vuln,secret,config --severity HIGH,CRITICAL --exit-code 1 .

What it does

Scans the repository for:

dependency vulnerabilities

accidental secrets

configuration issues



---

5. Generate a source SBOM locally

syft dir:. -o spdx-json > source-sbom.spdx.json

What it does

Builds a software bill of materials for the checked-out source tree.


---

6. Render and verify Helm charts locally

./ci/scripts/verify-helm.sh

What it does

lints the chart

renders dev, stage, and prod manifests

fails fast on template or values errors



---

7. Build backend and frontend images locally

docker build -f backend/Dockerfile -t fullstack-backend:test .
docker build -f frontend/Dockerfile -t fullstack-frontend:test .

What it does

Builds local versions of the runtime images for testing.


---

8. Scan built images locally

trivy image --severity HIGH,CRITICAL --exit-code 1 fullstack-backend:test
trivy image --severity HIGH,CRITICAL --exit-code 1 fullstack-frontend:test

What it does

Scans the exact image artifacts for high/critical vulnerabilities.


---

9. Generate image SBOMs locally

syft fullstack-backend:test -o spdx-json > backend-image-sbom.spdx.json
syft fullstack-frontend:test -o spdx-json > frontend-image-sbom.spdx.json

What it does

Generates SBOMs for the container images themselves.


---

10. Update GitOps overlay manually for emergency controlled workflow

Normally CI automates this, but the same action can be done carefully:

git clone git@github.com:examplecorp/gitops-repo.git
cd gitops-repo
yq -i '.backend.image.tag = "2.8.4-a1b2c3d"' apps/fullstack-app/overlays/prod/values.yaml
yq -i '.frontend.image.tag = "2.8.4-a1b2c3d"' apps/fullstack-app/overlays/prod/values.yaml
git add apps/fullstack-app/overlays/prod/values.yaml
git commit -m "Promote fullstack-app to prod: 2.8.4-a1b2c3d"
git push

What it does

Creates the desired-state change that GitOps will later reconcile.

Important: This is still Git-based change control, not direct deployment.


---

H. Production best practices

1. Keep CI and CD separate

CI builds artifacts. GitOps reconciles deployments. Do not collapse the two.


---

2. Use ephemeral agents only

This reduces drift and security exposure.


---

3. Tag images immutably

Never use latest. Use semver + SHA and keep the digest.


---

4. Always archive SBOMs and scan reports

These are valuable evidence and incident-response assets.


---

5. Fail builds on critical quality/security gates

At minimum:

failed tests

failed build

high/critical image issues according to policy

broken Helm rendering



---

6. Build once, promote the same artifact

Do not rebuild a separate “prod version” from the same commit later. Promote the already-built artifact by tag/digest.

This is a major enterprise principle.


---

7. Use GitOps repo changes as the only deployment handoff

That keeps release history visible and auditable.


---

8. Prefer PR-based promotion for stage and prod

Even when automated, opening a PR for promotion gives:

review

approvals

policy checks

clearer audit trail



---

9. Lock down CI credentials

The Jenkins agent role should have only the minimal AWS and Git permissions needed.


---

10. Treat scan policy as a managed product

Not every vulnerability should necessarily hard-fail forever without exception handling, but exception handling must be formal, time-bound, and reviewable.


---

11. Standardize pipeline libraries

Shared libraries reduce copy-paste pipeline sprawl and improve governance.


---

12. Measure CI performance

Track:

queue wait time

stage duration

flaky test rate

failed builds by cause

mean time to green


This matters in large enterprises.


---

13. Replicate artifacts for DR

Ensure images are available region-locally in the failover region.


---

I. Common enterprise mistakes

1. Jenkins directly deploying with kubectl

This breaks GitOps, weakens auditability, and creates hidden drift.


---

2. Rebuilding for each environment

That produces environment-specific artifacts and weakens release integrity.

Build once, promote many.


---

3. Using long-lived VM agents

These become fragile and insecure over time.


---

4. Not storing image digests

Without digests, rollback and provenance get weaker.


---

5. Scanning only source or only images

Both matter.


---

6. Ignoring Helm validation in CI

Broken templates then show up only at deployment time.


---

7. No SBOM generation

That is now a visible gap in many enterprise supply-chain programs.


---

8. Mutating deployment manifests outside Git

This creates invisible drift.


---

9. Too-broad Jenkins IAM roles

CI often becomes overprivileged if not intentionally constrained.


---

10. Promotion by copying files manually

This introduces human error and inconsistent release handling.


---

11. No branch or release policy discipline

Without clear promotion rules, environments become noisy and hard to reason about.


---

12. Pipeline sprawl with every team inventing its own logic

This weakens security consistency and slows platform evolution.


---

J. Interview explanation (Senior/Principal level)

A strong Principal-level explanation would sound like this:

> My CI design treats Jenkins as the artifact factory and policy enforcement layer, not the deployment engine. The pipeline runs linting, unit tests, Helm validation, Trivy scans, and SBOM generation, then builds immutable backend and frontend images and pushes them to ECR with traceable version tags and recorded digests. Instead of deploying directly, the pipeline updates the GitOps repository for the target environment, which preserves separation of duties and gives a clean audit trail. The design uses ephemeral Kubernetes agents, least-privilege IRSA roles, and a build-once-promote-many model so the exact same artifact moves from dev to stage to prod.



What makes this Principal-level

1. You frame CI as supply-chain control

Not just automation. A release governance system.

2. You separate artifact promotion from deployment execution

This is a key maturity signal.

3. You emphasize provenance and auditability

Commit → build → image → digest → GitOps commit → deployment.

4. You design for scale

Ephemeral agents, shared libraries, parallel stages, and policy standardization all show organizational thinking, not one-team scripting.

5. You understand release integrity

The strongest pattern is:

build once

sign/scan once

promote the same immutable artifact


That is much stronger than “rebuild on each environment.”

Good trade-off discussion

Jenkins vs GitHub Actions/GitLab CI

Jenkins is still valid in large enterprises because:

deep plugin ecosystem

strong shared-library pattern

easy hybrid environment integration

mature enterprise adoption


But it requires more platform ownership than newer SaaS CI systems.

Kaniko vs Docker-in-Docker

Kaniko reduces privileged daemon exposure and is often a better fit for Kubernetes-native CI.

Tag vs digest in GitOps

Use both for human clarity and immutable truth, with digest preferred as deployment truth in prod.


---
